# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Audit Log Middleware and Backend

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement API server audit logging: the audit event creation from requests, the audit policy evaluation, the audit backend dispatch (log file vs webhook), and the audit truncation for large request/response bodies.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I've successfully created a comprehensive analysis of the Kubernetes API server audit logging implementation. The answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` contains:

## Summary of Findings

**19 Go Source Files** identified across four main areas:

1. **Audit Event Creation** (4 files):
   - Filters that initialize audit context and capture request/response data
   - Request metadata and body logging functions

2. **Audit Policy Evaluation** (3 files):
   - Policy rule evaluation engine
   - Policy file loading and matching logic

3. **Audit Backend System** (7 files):
   - Backend interfaces (Backend, Sink)
   - Union backend for combining multiple outputs
   - Log file backend with JSON/legacy format support
   - Webhook backend with exponential backoff retries
   - Buffered backend for asynchronous batching
   - Truncation backend for large events

4. **Configuration & Types** (5 files):
   - Server options for assembling audit components
   - Audit event type definitions (internal and v1)

**Key Features:**
- **Policy-based filtering** - Evaluates rules by users, groups, verbs, namespaces, and resources
- **Multiple output destinations** - Log files and webhooks dispatched via Union backend
- **Event batching** - Buffered backend with configurable batch sizes and throttling
- **Automatic truncation** - Removes request/response bodies from oversized events while preserving metadata
- **Request lifecycle tracking** - Captures events at RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, and Panic stages

The complete flow document describes how requests flow through the audit system from initialization through policy evaluation, backend dispatch, optional truncation, and final output.

Audit Event Creation from Requests\\n\\nThe audit event creation process starts with HTTP request filters that initialize and capture audit information:\\n\\n**Request Initialization & ID Generation:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go:WithAuditInit` - Initializes audit context with a unique audit ID for each request. If the client doesn't provide an Audit-ID header, a new UUID is generated. The audit ID is echoed back in the response header.\\n\\n**Main Audit Filter:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go:WithAudit` - The primary audit filter decorator that wraps HTTP handlers. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nThe audit policy system determines which requests should be audited and at what level:\\n\\n**Policy Evaluation:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/evaluator.go:PolicyRuleEvaluator` - Interface that evaluates audit policy rules against request attributes.\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/checker.go:NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` - Creates a policy rule evaluator from an audit policy.\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/checker.go:EvaluatePolicyRule` - Evaluates each policy rule by checking users, groups, verbs, namespaces, resources, and non-resource URLs. Returns the audit level (None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse) and stages to omit.\\n\\n**Policy File Handling:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/reader.go:LoadPolicyFromFile` - Reads and parses the audit policy YAML file.\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/util.go` - Utility functions for policy matching including pattern matching for URLs and resource wildcards.\\n\\n## 3. Every backend must implement ProcessEvents, Run, Shutdown, and String().\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/types.go:Sink` - Interface with ProcessEvents(events) method for handling audit events.\\n\\n**Union Backend (Multi-Backend Dispatch):**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/union.go:Union` - Creates a composite backend that sends events to multiple backends sequentially. Allows combining log file and webhook backends.\\n\\n**Log File Backend:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go:NewBackend` - Creates a log file backend that writes audit events to a file.\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go:ProcessEvents` - Encodes and writes events in either legacy (1-line text) or JSON format.\\n\\n**Webhook Backend:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go:NewBackend` - Creates a webhook backend configured from a file.\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go:NewDynamicBackend` - Creates a webhook backend from a REST client for dynamic webhook configuration.\\n- The webhook backend sends audit events via HTTP POST requests to external audit services with exponential backoff retry logic.\\n\\n**Buffered Backend (Event Batching):**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go:NewBackend` - Wraps a delegate backend with buffering and batching capabilities.\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go:ProcessEvents` - Collects events into batches and sends them to the delegate backend asynchronously or synchronously based on configuration. Supports batching modes (batch, blocking, blocking-strict) with throttling.\\n\\n## 4. Audit Truncation for Large Events\\n\\nThe truncation system prevents oversized events from being lost:\\n\\n**Truncation Backend:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go:NewBackend` - Creates a truncating backend that wraps a delegate backend.\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go:ProcessEvents` - Checks event size and batch size against configured limits. If an event exceeds MaxEventSize, it calls the truncate() function.\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go:truncate` - Removes RequestObject and ResponseObject from oversized events while preserving metadata. Adds an annotation 'audit.k8s.io/truncated: true' to indicate truncation.\\n\\n## 5. Audit Configuration & Wiring\\n\\nThe server options package assembles and configures all audit components:\\n\\n**Audit Options:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go:AuditOptions` - Configuration struct for audit settings (policy file, log options, webhook options).\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go:AuditLogOptions` - Configuration for log file backend (path, max age, max backups, format, batching, truncation).\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go:AuditWebhookOptions` - Configuration for webhook backend (config file, retry backoff, batching, truncation).\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go:AuditBatchOptions` - Configuration for batching mode (batch size, max wait, throttling).\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go:AuditTruncateOptions` - Configuration for event truncation (enabled flag, max event size, max batch size).\\n\\n**Backend Assembly:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go:ApplyTo` - Main method that assembles the complete audit system:\\n  1. Creates the policy rule evaluator from the policy file\\n  2. Creates the log backend (if enabled)\\n  3. Creates the webhook backend (if enabled)\\n  4. Wraps the webhook backend with truncation and buffering\\n  5. Combines backends using the Union function\\n  6. Sets the AuditBackend and AuditPolicyRuleEvaluator in the server config\\n\\n**Policy Loading:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go:newPolicyRuleEvaluator` - Loads policy from file and creates a policy evaluator.\\n\\n## 6. Audit Event Types\\n\\n**Internal API Types:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/apis/audit/types.go` - Internal audit event types including Event struct with stage, level, user info, object references, request/response objects.\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/apis/audit/v1/types.go` - v1 audit event schema for serialization.\\n\\n## Complete Request Flow\\n\\n1. **WithAuditInit** initializes the audit context and generates/receives an audit ID\\n2. **WithAudit** decorator intercepts the request\\n3. **evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent** evaluates the policy and initializes the audit context\\n4. **LogRequestMetadata** captures request details\\n5. At each stage (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete), **ProcessEventStage** sends the event to the backend(s)\\n6. **Union** backend optionally routes to multiple backends\\n7. **Truncate** backend checks size and truncates if needed\\n8. **Buffered** backend batches events before dispatching\\n9. **Log** and **Webhook** backends process the final events\\n\\nThis architecture provides flexible, scalable audit logging with policy-based filtering, multiple output formats, and automatic event truncation for large payloads.\"\n}\n",
